## lattice-system

A Lean 4 + Mathlib formalization project targeting general lattice models.
This project subsumes and generalizes the earlier
[ising-model](https://github.com/phasetr/ising-model) project, progressively
covering classical spin systems, quantum spin systems, Hubbard, BCS,
CAR algebras, and eventually lattice QCD.

## Design axis: graphs, not lattices

Despite the name, the **primary combinatorial abstraction in this
library is a graph `(╬ø, E_╬ø)`** ÔÇö finite for finite-volume work and
infinite for the thermodynamic-limit / algebraic-formulation work
that is a major long-term goal ÔÇö not "a lattice". Concrete lattices
(the 1D chain, square / cubic grids, infinite chains, Ôäñ^d, ÔÇĞ) appear
only as specific instances such as `SimpleGraph.pathGraph`,
`SimpleGraph.cycleGraph`, products of these, or their infinite
analogues. This convention follows the standard mathematical-physics
literature on many-body systems on graphs (Lieb's theorem on
bipartite lattices, the MarshallÔÇôLiebÔÇôMattis theorem, Miyao 2021
┬ğ3, ÔÇĞ) and aligns the project with mathlib's `SimpleGraph`
foundations.

Finite-volume work uses `╬ø : Type*` together with `[Fintype ╬ø]`
when needed (e.g. for traces, partition functions, finite sums of
local terms); infinite-volume work drops the `Fintype` assumption
and uses graphs over types like `Ôäñ` or `Ôäñ^d` instead.

The bridge from a `SimpleGraph` to the pairwise coupling
`J : ╬ø ÔåÆ ╬ø ÔåÆ Ôäé` consumed by `heisenbergHamiltonian` (and similar
operators) lives in `LatticeSystem.Lattice.Graph` (`couplingOf`).
Existing chain coupling families (`openChainCoupling`,
`periodicChainCoupling`) are characterised as
`couplingOf (pathGraph _) _` and `couplingOf (cycleGraph _) _`
respectively.

## Scope

| Area | Stage | Typical references |
|---|---|---|
| Classical spin systems | Inherited from ising-model | Friedli-Velenik, Glimm-Jaffe |
| Quantum spin systems | Current focus | Tasaki, Nielsen-Chuang (cross-check) |
| Hubbard / BCS | Medium term | Tasaki 1998, Bru-Pedra |
| CAR-algebraic formulation | Medium-long term | Araki-Moriya, Bru-Pedra |
| Thermodynamic limit (infinite graphs) | Long term, **major project goal** | Simon, Friedli-Velenik, Bratteli-Robinson |
| Lattice QCD | Longest term | Aarts, Davies |

## Refactoring conventions and review criteria

A **single-source-of-truth document** for refactoring conventions
applied as the review checklist on every pull request:
[Refactoring conventions and review criteria](refactoring-conventions.html).
Topics: test methods (decide / bridge / small-exhaustive / shim /
`#guard_msgs`), module-split criteria, generic / dedup conventions,
deprecation window policy, naming / docstring rules, linter
exceptions, public-doc synchronisation.

The companion page [Deprecation window](deprecations.html) tracks
currently-deprecated public declarations, the `since` date,
recommended replacement, and earliest-removal window.

| P1i (Tasaki ┬ğ2.4) | Heisenberg Hamiltonian on the fully-polarised state: `H |sÔÇĞsÔş® = (Ôêæ_{x,y} J(x,y)┬À(if x=y then 3/4 else 1/4)) ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®` (eq. (2.4.5), `S = 1/2`); plus the ladder step `┼£_tot^┬▒ ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®` preserves the same H-eigenvalue (eqs. (2.4.7) operator-level), the single-axis rotated constant-spin state `├ø^(╬▒)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®` shares the H-eigenvalue, and the two-axis spin-coherent state `├ø^(3)_¤ò ├ø^(2)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş® = |╬Ş_╬©,¤òÔş®` (eq. (2.4.6) for `s = 0`); plus the magnetic-quantum-number labelling `┼£tot^(3) ┬À (┼£tot^-)^k ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş® = (Smax - k) ┬À (┼£tot^-)^k ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş®` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, lowering from highest weight) and its dual `┼£tot^(3) ┬À (┼£tot^+)^k ┬À |Ôåô..ÔåôÔş® = (-Smax + k) ┬À (┼£tot^+)^k ┬À |Ôåô..ÔåôÔş®` (eq. (2.4.9), unnormalised, raising from lowest weight); plus the Casimir invariance `┼£tot┬▓ ┬À (┼£tot^Ôêô)^k ┬À |s..sÔş® = Smax(Smax+1) ┬À (┼£tot^Ôêô)^k ┬À |s..sÔş®` for any constant `s`. For the matched highest/lowest-weight ladders, the unnormalised iterates `(┼£tot^-)^k ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş®` and `(┼£tot^+)^k ┬À |Ôåô..ÔåôÔş®` carry `(H, ┼£tot┬▓, ┼£tot^(3))` simultaneous eigenvalues `(c_J, Smax(Smax+1), SmaxÔêôk)`; plus the boundary annihilations `┼£tot^- ┬À |Ôåô..ÔåôÔş® = 0` and `┼£tot^+ ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş® = 0` ensuring the ladder terminates after spanning all `2Smax + 1 = |╬ø| + 1` magnetisation sectors ÔÇö building toward the full |╬Ğ_MÔş® / |╬Ş_╬©,¤òÔş® ferromagnetic ground-state space | Done |
| P1g | Gibbs state `¤ü = e^{-╬▓H}/Z`, `Tr(¤ü) = 1`, `Ôş¿1Ôş® = 1`, `Z(0) = dim`, `Z(0) Ôëá 0`, linearity `Ôş¿OÔéü+OÔééÔş® = Ôş¿OÔéüÔş®+Ôş¿OÔééÔş®`, `Ôş¿c┬ÀOÔş® = c┬ÀÔş¿OÔş®`, `Ôş¿-OÔş® = -Ôş¿OÔş®`, `Ôş¿AÔêÆBÔş® = Ôş¿AÔş®ÔêÆÔş¿BÔş®`, `Ôş¿╬ú fÔş® = ╬ú Ôş¿fÔş®`, `[¤ü, H] = 0`, reality of `Ôş¿OÔş®` for Hermitian `O`, conservation `Ôş¿[H,A]Ôş® = 0`, anticommutator real / commutator imaginary, `(Ôş¿H┬ÀOÔş®).im = 0`, ╬▓ = 0 closed form `¤ü_0 = I/dim` and `Ôş¿AÔş®_0 = Tr A / dim`, one-parameter group property `e^{-(╬▓Ôéü+╬▓Ôéé)H} = e^{-╬▓ÔéüH} ┬À e^{-╬▓ÔééH}` and invertibility, exact discrete semigroup identity `e^{-(n╬▓)H} = (e^{-╬▓H})^n` (extended to `n : Ôäñ` via `gibbsExp_inv`) | Done |

| P1j (Tasaki ┬ğ2.3) | Single-spin and multi-spin time-reversal map `╬İ╠é := ├╗_2 ┬À K╠é` for `S = 1/2`: explicit formula `╬İ╠é((a, b)ßÁÇ) = (-b*, a*)ßÁÇ` (Tasaki eq. (2.3.8) at half-odd-integer spin), spin sign flip `╬İ╠é(┼£^(╬▒) v) = -┼£^(╬▒)(╬İ╠é v)` (Tasaki eq. (2.3.14)), and multi-spin Kramers `╬İ╠é_tot┬▓ = (-1)^|╬ø| ┬À 1╠é` for finite `╬ø` (Tasaki ┬ğ2.3 lattice extension at `S = 1/2`) | Done |

`H_0`, per-bond `┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y ┬À |╬Ğ_N├®elÔş® = (1/2)|swapÔş® - (1/4)|╬Ğ_N├®elÔş®` for every adjacent and wrap-around bond (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.3)), per-bond expectation `Ôş¿╬Ğ_N├®el, ┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y ┬À ╬Ğ_N├®elÔş® = -(1/4)` (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.4) ingredient), per-bond `┼£^z ┬À ┼£^z` correlation `-(1/4)` and off-diagonal correlator vanishing, parallel-bond expectation `+1/4`, K=1 chain Heisenberg energy `J/2`, time-reversal `╬İ╠é_tot ┬À |╬Ğ_N├®elÔş®` action across all dimensions, Marshall sign machinery (generic `marshallSignOf` + chain / 2D / 3D specialisations + `flipConfig` + Marshall ├ù time-reversal bridge), the **generic graph-centric `neelStateOf : (V ÔåÆ Bool) ÔåÆ ((V ÔåÆ Fin 2) ÔåÆ Ôäé)`** primitive (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.2) graph-centric form) of which the chain / 2D / 3D versions are 1-line corollaries via the `_eq_neelConfigOf` / `_eq_neelStateOf` bridges, the **Marshall-dressed standard basis** `marshallDressedBasis A ¤â := marshallSignOf A ¤â ÔÇó basisVec ¤â` (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.8)) with orthonormality and `H_M`-membership, the **realness of dressed Heisenberg matrix elements** for real coupling `J` (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 p. 41, Property (i): each `((spinHalfDot x y) ¤â ¤â').im = 0`, hence `((heisenbergHamiltonian J) ¤â ¤â').im = 0`, hence the dressed bilinear pairing has zero imaginary part), the **Marshall sign trick** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 p. 41, Property (ii)): for real non-negative `J` supported on bipartite bonds and `¤â Ôëá ¤â'`, the dressed off-diagonal Heisenberg pairing has non-positive real part, the **swap-connectivity** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 p. 41ÔÇô42, Property (iii)): for a connected graph `G` and any `¤â x Ôëá ¤â y`, the configurations `¤â` and `basisSwap ¤â x y` are connected by a chain of single-edge swaps, and the **MarshallÔÇôLiebÔÇôMattis Theorem 2.2 in `H_0` (matrix level)**: assembled across PRs ╬▒-5a through ╬▒-5o, the shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `B = c ┬À I ÔêÆ M` (symmetric, non-negative, irreducible on `H_0`) admits a unique-up-to-positive-scalar strictly positive PerronÔÇôFrobenius eigenvector ÔÇö equivalent to the matrix-level Tasaki (2.5.4) ground-state expansion `╬ú_¤â c_¤â \|╬¿╠â^¤âÔş®` with `c_¤â > 0` ÔÇö first five steps of the MarshallÔÇôLiebÔÇôMattis Theorem 2.2 formalization track (Issue #412) | In progress |
| P1l (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5, 2D / 3D Heisenberg) | 2D square-lattice + 2D torus + 3D cubic-lattice Heisenberg Hamiltonians via graph products `pathGraph (N+1) Ôûí pathGraph (N+1)` and `cycleGraph (N+2) Ôûí cycleGraph (N+2)`; Hermiticity + Gibbs state companion families (full 11-companion family per variant: `_isHermitian`, `_commute_hamiltonian`, `_GibbsExpectation_zero`, `_im_of_isHermitian`, `_commutator_hamiltonian`, `_mul_hamiltonian_im`, `_hamiltonian_sq_im`, `_hamiltonian_pow_im`, `_anticommutator_im`, `_commutator_re`, `_HamiltonianVariance_im`, `_partitionFn_im`, `_ofReal_re_eq`, `_pow_trace`) at parity with the 1D open / periodic chain | Done |
| P1m (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5, generic-S sector form) | **Spin-S MarshallÔÇôLiebÔÇôMattis Theorem 2.2 on the magnetization sector**: generalisation of P1k from spin-1/2 / `H_0` to general spin `S` (`N = 2S`) and arbitrary magnetization sector `M` via the subtype `magConfigS V N M`. Bipartite raise/lower reachability (╬│-3 connectivity for general spin) lifted to the sector subtype. PF application: `IsIrreducible` (#846), positive Perron eigenvector existence (#847) and uniqueness (#848) on the shifted sector matrix. Marshall sign conjugation forward (#853) + inverse (#854) gives a real-form sector eigenvector existence with Marshall sign structure. Eigenvector uniqueness (#854) at fixed `╬╝` and eigenvalue uniqueness (#856, via dressed-sector symmetry + Rayleigh identity). Bundled real-form ground-state theorems: same-`╬╝` form (#855) and forced-eigenvalue form (#859). Complex-form bridge: complex sector matrix Hermiticity + real-Ôåö-complex eigenvector correspondence (#857, #858, #861). Complex-form existence (#860), Marshall-positive uniqueness (#862), and **strongest bundled COMPLEX ground-state theorem** `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` (#865) ÔÇö the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the magnetization sector. Generic spin `S`, arbitrary bipartite-antiferromagnetic Heisenberg coupling supported on a connected bipartite graph, with the intermediate-existence hypothesis. The next step is the lift from the magnetization sector to the FULL Hilbert space ÔÇö comparing ground-state energies across magnetization sectors. | Done |
| P2 | Finite-volume Hubbard / BCS | In progress (single-mode CAR algebra; multi-mode JordanÔÇôWigner backbone: JW string + multi-mode `c_i`, `c_iÔÇá` definitions and Hermiticity, `c_0` reductions, full on-site CAR `c_i┬▓ = 0`, `(c_iÔÇá)┬▓ = 0`, `{c_i, c_iÔÇá} = 1`, adjoint `(c_i)ß┤┤ = c_iÔÇá`, JW string idempotent `J┬▓ = 1`, site-occupation number operator `n_i` with Hermiticity and idempotency; **full cross-site CAR algebra `{c_i, c_j} = 0`, `{c_iÔÇá, c_jÔÇá} = 0`, `{c_i, c_jÔÇá} = 0`, `{c_iÔÇá, c_j} = 0` for every `i < j`**; **Hubbard chain (open + periodic BC), Hermiticity + full Gibbs companion family**; **U(1)├ùU(1) spin symmetry: `[N_Ôåæ, H] = [N_Ôåô, H] = [S^z_tot, H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬ğ9.3.3)**; **full SU(2) spin symmetry: `[┼£^+_tot, H] = [┼£^-_tot, H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬ğ9.3.3)**; **all-up-spin state `hubbardAllUpState`: complete kinetic/interaction sector; Casimir `(┼£_tot)┬▓`; eigenvalue `S_max(S_max+1)`; Definition 11.1 `isSaturatedFerromagnet` (Tasaki ┬ğ11.1.1 / eq. (10.1.5))**; **SU(2) algebra: `[┼£^z, ┼£^-] = -┼£^-`, eigenvalue preservation and decrement by `┼£^-` (Tasaki ┬ğ9.3.3, ┬ğ11.1.1)**) |
| P3 | CAR algebras, quasi-local C*-algebras, KMS states | Not started |
| P4 | Thermodynamic limit, phase transitions | Not started |

## Formalized theorems

All items below are formally proved with **zero `sorry`**. Full
mathematical statements and proof sketches are in
[`tex/proof-guide.tex`](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/blob/main/tex/proof-guide.tex).

### Single-site Pauli operators

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ2.1 eq. (2.1.8), p. 15. Cross-checked with Nielsen-Chuang
┬ğ2.1.3 Figure 2.2 (pp. 65-66, definitions), Ex. 2.19 (p. 70,
Hermiticity), Ex. 2.41 (p. 78, `(¤â^╬▒)┬▓ = I` and anticommutation),
Ex. 2.40 (p. 77, commutator, whence the cyclic products).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `pauliX/Y/Z_isHermitian` | `(¤â^╬▒)ÔÇá = ¤â^╬▒` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX/Y/Z_mul_self` | `(¤â^╬▒)┬▓ = I` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_mul_pauliY` etc. | `¤â^x ¤â^y = i┬À¤â^z` (cyclic) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_anticomm_pauliY` etc. | `¤â^╬▒ ¤â^╬▓ + ¤â^╬▓ ¤â^╬▒ = 0` (╬▒ Ôëá ╬▓) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 operators (Tasaki ┬ğ2.1)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ2.1 eqs. (2.1.1), (2.1.7), (2.1.8), pp. 13-15.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfOp1/2/3` | `┼£^(╬▒) := ¤â^(╬▒) / 2` (Tasaki (2.1.7)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `pauliX_eq_two_smul_spinHalfOp1` etc. | `¤â^(╬▒) = 2 ┬À ┼£^(╬▒)` (Tasaki (2.1.8)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_isHermitian` etc. | `┼£^(╬▒)` is Hermitian | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_mul_self` etc. | `(┼£^(╬▒))┬▓ = (1/4) ┬À I` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_anticomm_spinHalfOp2` etc. | anticommutation at `╬▒ Ôëá ╬▓` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalfOp1_commutator_spinHalfOp2` etc. | `[┼£^(╬▒), ┼£^(╬▓)] = i ┬À ┼£^(╬│)` (Tasaki (2.1.1)) | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |
| `spinHalf_total_spin_squared` | `╬ú (┼£^(╬▒))┬▓ = (3/4) ┬À I`, i.e. `S(S+1)` with `S=1/2` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |

### ZÔéé ├ù ZÔéé representation (Tasaki ┬ğ2.1 eqs. (2.1.27)-(2.1.34))

The ZÔéé ├ù ZÔéé structure is proved across files:
- S = 1/2 (projective, eq. (2.1.31)): `spinHalfRot*_pi_sq = -1`, anticommutation, products.
- S = 1 (genuine, eq. (2.1.27)): `spinOnePiRot*_sq = 1`, commutation.

See `Quantum/Z2Z2.lean` for the unified documentation.

### Spin-`S` operators (general S ÔëÑ 0, parameterised by `N = 2S : Ôäò`)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body Systems*, ┬ğ2.1 Problem 2.1.a (p. 15) and solution S.1 (p. 493).

Generic spin-`S` operators live on `Matrix (Fin (N + 1)) (Fin (N + 1)) Ôäé`, with `N = 2S : Ôäò` (so `N = 1` Ôçö `S = 1/2`, `N = 2` Ôçö `S = 1`). Tracking issue #458 (Tasaki ┬ğ2.1 P1d''' general-S generalisation).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinSOp3` | `┼£^(3) := diag(N/2, N/2 - 1, ÔÇĞ, -N/2)` for `N : Ôäò` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus` / `spinSOpMinus` | raising/lowering operators with matrix entries `ÔêÜ(k┬À(N ÔêÆ k + 1))` (resp. `ÔêÜ((N ÔêÆ k)(k + 1))`) on the immediate sub/super-diagonal | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp1` / `spinSOp2` | `┼£^(1) := (┼£^+ + ┼£^-) / 2`, `┼£^(2) := (┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-) / (2 i)` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_apply_top` / `_bottom` | `┼£^+` annihilates `\|NÔş®` (highest weight); `┼£^-` annihilates `\|0Ôş®` (lowest weight) ÔÇö the ladder boundaries | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp{Plus,Minus}` | **Cartan relations** `[┼£^{(3)}, ┼£^+] = ┼£^+` and `[┼£^{(3)}, ┼£^-] = -┼£^-`: `┼£^┬▒` shift the magnetic quantum number by `┬▒1`. Proved entry-wise via `Matrix.diagonal_mul` / `mul_diagonal` (╬▓-2 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Algebra.lean` |
| `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_conjTranspose` / `spinSOp{1,2,3}_isHermitian` | adjointness `(┼£^+)ß┤┤ = ┼£^-`, `(┼£^-)ß┤┤ = ┼£^+`, and Hermiticity of `┼£^{(╬▒)}` for `╬▒ Ôêê {1, 2, 3}` (╬▓-3 of Issue #458). The ladder adjointness follows from the matrix-entry symmetry; `┼£^{(1)}` and `┼£^{(2)}` use the `1/2` and `1/(2i)` self-conjugacy facts | `Quantum/SpinS/Hermitian.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj` / `spinSOp3_sub_smul_mul_diagProj` / `_self_mul_diagProj` | the **diagonal projector** `P_k := diag(╬┤_{i,k})` and the eigenvalue-action lemma `(┼£^{(3)} ÔêÆ ╬╗_j ÔÇó 1) ┬À P_k = (╬╗_k ÔêÆ ╬╗_j) ┬À P_k`, with the annihilation specialisation at `j = k` (╬▓-4 of Issue #458). Foundation for the Lagrange-interpolation polynomial decomposition: each `P_k` will be expressed as `ÔêÅ_{j Ôëá k} (┼£^{(3)} ÔêÆ ╬╗_j ÔÇó 1) / (╬╗_k ÔêÆ ╬╗_j)` in a follow-up PR | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProj.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mul_diagProj` / `diagProj_mul_spinSOp3` / `spinSOp3_commute_diagProj` | the **eigenvalue equation** `┼£^{(3)} ┬À P_k = ╬╗_k ┬À P_k` (where `╬╗_k = (N : Ôäé)/2 ÔêÆ k`), with the symmetric `P_k ┬À ┼£^{(3)} = ╬╗_k ┬À P_k` and the resulting commutativity. Both are diagonal-times-diagonal computations (╬▓-5 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Lagrange.lean` |
| `mul_diagProj_apply` / `diagProj_mul_apply` / `spinSOp{Plus,Minus}_mul_diagProj_apply` | **Column/row selection** by the diagonal projector: `(A ┬À P_k)[i, j] = A[i, k]` if `j = k` else `0` (and dually for `P_k ┬À A`). Specialised to `┼£^┬▒` produces off-diagonal matrix units (╬▓-6 of Issue #458) ÔÇö the building blocks of the polynomial decomposition theorem | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderProj.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_mul_spinSOpMinus` | **Ladder recursion**: `┼£^+ ┬À P_{k+1} ┬À ┼£^- = (k + 1)(N ÔêÆ k) ┬À P_k`. The triple product collapses to a non-zero scalar multiple of `P_k`. Iterating from the lowest-weight projector `P_N` (itself a polynomial in `┼£^{(3)}`) yields every diagonal projector as a polynomial in `{1╠é, ┼£^{(╬▒)}}` (╬▓-7 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderRecursion.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_first` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_last` | **Ladder boundaries**: `┼£^+ ┬À P_0 = 0` (top of ladder) and `┼£^- ┬À P_N = 0` (bottom). The first/last columns of `┼£^┬▒` vanish, so multiplication by `P_{0/N}` (which selects that column) gives `0`. Terminate the recursion at the highest- and lowest-weight projectors (╬▓-8 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderBoundary.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_isHermitian` / `sum_spinSDiagProj_eq_one` | **Hermiticity** of each `P_k`, and the **resolution of the identity** `╬ú_k P_k = 1`. The latter is the cornerstone for the matrix-unit decomposition: combined with the off-diagonal matrix units (╬▓-6, ╬▓-7), gives every matrix in `M_{N+1}(Ôäé)` (╬▓-9 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjProperties.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_diagProj_succ_eq_single` / `spinSOpMinus_mul_diagProj_eq_single` | **Off-diagonal matrix-unit decomposition**: `┼£^+ ┬À P_{i+1} = ÔêÜ((i+1)(NÔêÆi)) ┬À E_{i, i+1}` and `┼£^- ┬À P_i = ÔêÜ((NÔêÆi)(i+1)) ┬À E_{i+1, i}`, where `E_{a, b} := Matrix.single a b 1` is the (a, b) matrix unit (╬▓-10 of Issue #458). These are the simplest off-diagonal matrix units expressible via `┼£^┬▒` ladder action on diagonal projectors | `Quantum/SpinS/OffDiagUnit.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_sq_eq_diagonal` | `(┼£^{(3)})┬▓ = diag((N/2 ÔêÆ i)┬▓)`. Step toward the **Casimir identity** `(┼£^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼£^{(2)})┬▓ + (┼£^{(3)})┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬À 1` for general spin (╬▓-11 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Op3Square.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mul_spinSOpMinus_eq_diagonal` | `┼£^+ ┬À ┼£^- = diag((i + 1)(N ÔêÆ i))`. The product is diagonal because `┼£^+[i, l] ┬À ┼£^-[l, j]` is non-zero only when `l = i + 1 = j + 1`, forcing `i = j`. Combined with the analogous `┼£^- ┬À ┼£^+` and `(┼£^{(3)})┬▓`, this assembles the Casimir identity (╬▓-12 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PlusMinusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOpMinus_mul_spinSOpPlus_eq_diagonal` | `┼£^- ┬À ┼£^+ = diag(i ┬À (N ÔêÆ i + 1))`. Symmetric to ╬▓-12 with `┼£^┬▒` swapped (╬▓-13 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/MinusPlusDiag.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_sq_add_spinSOp2_sq` / `spinSOp_total_squared` | **Casimir identity** for general spin-`S`: `(┼£^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼£^{(2)})┬▓ + (┼£^{(3)})┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬À 1`, equivalent to `S(S+1) ┬À 1` for `S = N/2`. Proves the irreducible spin-`S` representation has Casimir eigenvalue `S(S+1)` (Schur's lemma). The intermediate identity `(┼£^{(1)})┬▓ + (┼£^{(2)})┬▓ = (1/2)(┼£^+ ┬À ┼£^- + ┼£^- ┬À ┼£^+)` is proved using `module` (╬▓-14 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Casimir.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_mulVec_basis` | spin-`S` eigenstate equation `┼£^{(3)} ┬À \|kÔş® = (N/2 ÔêÆ k) ┬À \|kÔş®`, where `\|kÔş® := Pi.single k 1` is the `k`-th unit basis vector of `(Fin (N + 1) ÔåÆ Ôäé)` (╬▓-15 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Eigenstates.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mulVec_basis` / `spinSOpMinus_mulVec_basis` | **Ladder action on basis vectors**: `┼£^+ ┬À \|kÔş® = ÔêÜ(k(N ÔêÆ k + 1)) ┬À \|k ÔêÆ 1Ôş®` for `k ÔëÑ 1`, and `┼£^- ┬À \|kÔş® = ÔêÜ((N ÔêÆ k)(k + 1)) ┬À \|k + 1Ôş®` for `k Ôëñ N ÔêÆ 1`. The standard SU(2) ladder relations on the magnetic-quantum-number basis (╬▓-16 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LadderStates.lean` |
| `spinSOp_total_squared_mulVec_basis` | **Casimir eigenvalue on basis**: `(┼£)┬▓ ┬À \|kÔş® = (N(N+2)/4) ┬À \|kÔş®`. Direct consequence of `(┼£)┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬À 1` (╬▓-14) ÔÇö every basis vector has the universal Casimir eigenvalue, reflecting that the spin-`S` representation is a single irreducible (Schur) (╬▓-17 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirEigenvalue.lean` |
| `spinSOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}_commute_total_squared` | **Casimir invariance**: each `┼£^{(╬▒)}` and `┼£^┬▒` commutes with the Casimir `(┼£)┬▓ = (N(N+2)/4) ┬À 1`. Direct consequence of the scalar nature of the Casimir (╬▓-18 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CasimirInvariance.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_commutator_spinSOpMinus` | **Third Cartan relation**: `[┼£^+, ┼£^-] = 2 ┬À ┼£^{(3)}`. Combines ╬▓-12 (`┼£^+ ┬À ┼£^- = diag((i + 1)(N ÔêÆ i))`) and ╬▓-13 (`┼£^- ┬À ┼£^+ = diag(i (N ÔêÆ i + 1))`); the difference `(i+1)(N-i) ÔêÆ i(N-i+1) = N ÔêÆ 2i = 2(N/2 ÔêÆ i)` matches `2 ┬À ┼£^{(3)}` (╬▓-19 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/Cartan3.lean` |
| `spinSOp1_commutator_spinSOp2` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}] = i ┬À ┼£^{(3)}`. Derived from the Cartan relations by algebraic manipulation through `┼£^{(1)} = (┼£^+ + ┼£^-)/2` and `┼£^{(2)} = (┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-)/(2i)`: `(P+Q)(P-Q) ÔêÆ (P-Q)(P+Q) = -2[P, Q] = -4 ┼£^{(3)}`, then scalar simplification `-1/I = I` (╬▓-20 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator.lean` |
| `spinSOp2_commutator_spinSOp3` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}] = i ┬À ┼£^{(1)}`. Derived from Cartan ╬▓-2 (`[┼£^{(3)}, ┼£^┬▒] = ┬▒┼£^┬▒`) via `┼£^{(2)} = (┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-)/(2i)`: the commutator reduces to `(1/(2i)) (-┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-) = (-1/(2i)) ┬À 2 ┼£^{(1)} = i ┬À ┼£^{(1)}` (╬▓-21 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator23.lean` |
| `spinSOp3_commutator_spinSOp1` | **Cyclic SU(2) commutator** `[┼£^{(3)}, ┼£^{(1)}] = i ┬À ┼£^{(2)}`. Derived from Cartan ╬▓-2 via `┼£^{(1)} = (┼£^+ + ┼£^-)/2`: the commutator reduces to `(1/2) (┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-) = (1/2) ┬À (2i) ┬À ┼£^{(2)} = i ┬À ┼£^{(2)}`. Together with ╬▓-20 and ╬▓-21 this completes the standard SU(2) commutator algebra (Tasaki eq. (2.1.1)) for spin-`S` operators (╬▓-22 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator31.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mul_self` / `spinSDiagProj_mul_of_ne` | **Idempotence and orthogonality** of the diagonal projectors `P_k = |kÔş®Ôş¿k|`: `P_k ┬À P_k = P_k` and `P_i ┬À P_j = 0` for `i Ôëá j`. Combined with ╬▓-9 (`Ôêæ_k P_k = 1`) this gives the spectral decomposition of the identity for `┼£^{(3)}` (╬▓-23 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjOrtho.lean` |
| `aeval_diagonal` | **Polynomial evaluation at a diagonal matrix**: `aeval (Matrix.diagonal v) p = Matrix.diagonal (fun i => p.eval (v i))`. Foundational lemma for the Lagrange-interpolation step (╬▓-25+) ÔÇö lets us pull a polynomial in `┼£^{(3)}` (a diagonal matrix) through to its scalar action on each diagonal entry. Proof by `Polynomial.induction_on'` on monomials and addition (╬▓-24 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AevalDiagonal.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_eq_lagrange_aeval` | **Lagrange-interpolation formula for `P_k`**: `P_k = aeval (┼£^{(3)}) (Lagrange.basis Finset.univ (spinSOp3Eigen N) k)`, equivalently `P_k = ÔêÅ_{j Ôëá k} (┼£^{(3)} ÔêÆ ╬╗_j ÔÇó 1)/(╬╗_k ÔêÆ ╬╗_j)` with `╬╗_j = (N : Ôäé)/2 ÔêÆ j.val`. Combines ╬▓-24 (`aeval` of diagonal) with mathlib's `Lagrange.eval_basis_self` / `eval_basis_of_ne`. Each diagonal projector is therefore a **polynomial in `┼£^{(3)}`**, which combined with ╬▓-9 (`Ôêæ P_k = 1`) gives an explicit polynomial decomposition of `1╠é` (╬▓-25 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LagrangeFormula.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_eq_one_add_I_smul_two` / `spinSOpMinus_eq_one_sub_I_smul_two` | **Inversion of the Cartesian definition**: `┼£^+ = ┼£^{(1)} + i ┬À ┼£^{(2)}` and `┼£^- = ┼£^{(1)} ÔêÆ i ┬À ┼£^{(2)}`. The defining identities `┼£^{(1)} = (1/2)(┼£^+ + ┼£^-)`, `┼£^{(2)} = (1/(2i))(┼£^+ ÔêÆ ┼£^-)` invert to express the ladder operators as **linear combinations** of the Hermitian Cartesian spin operators (╬▓-26 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMAsOneTwo.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin_spinSOp3` / `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin` | **Diagonal projectors live in the algebra generated by the spin operators**: `P_k Ôêê Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(3)}}` (and a fortiori `P_k Ôêê Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}}`). Promotes the Lagrange-interpolation formula (╬▓-25) from "polynomial-evaluation" form to "subalgebra-membership" form via `Algebra.adjoin_singleton_eq_range_aeval` (╬▓-27 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/ProjMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_mem_adjoin` / `spinSOpMinus_mem_adjoin` | **Ladder operators live in `Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(╬▒)}}`**: `┼£^+, ┼£^- Ôêê Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}}`. Direct consequence of ╬▓-26 (`┼£^┬▒ = ┼£^{(1)} ┬▒ i ┬À ┼£^{(2)}`) and the fact that subalgebras are closed under `Ôäé`-linear combinations (╬▓-28 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMMemAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Immediate-neighbor matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(╬▒)}}`**: `E_{i, i+1}, E_{i+1, i} Ôêê Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}}`. Combines ╬▓-10 (`┼£^+ ┬À P_{i+1} = ÔêÜ((i+1)(N-i)) ┬À E_{i, i+1}`) with ╬▓-27 (`P_k Ôêê adjoin`) and ╬▓-28 (`┼£^┬▒ Ôêê adjoin`); the ladder coefficient is non-zero on the valid range and the subalgebra is closed under multiplication and scalar `smul`. Step toward expressing every matrix unit as a polynomial in `{┼£^{(╬▒)}}` (╬▓-29 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/NeighborUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `single_offset_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_offset_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Arbitrary stride-(k+1) matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(╬▒)}}`**: `E_{i, i+(k+1)}, E_{i+(k+1), i} Ôêê Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(╬▒)}}` for any `k`. Induction on `k`: base case is ╬▓-29; inductive step chains via `Matrix.single_mul_single_same` (`E_{i,j} ┬À E_{j,k} = E_{i,k}`) (╬▓-30 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/OffsetUnitAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_single_mem_adjoin` | **Every matrix unit `E_{i,j}` lives in `Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(╬▒)}}`**. Three-case split: `i = j` reduces to ╬▓-27 via `Matrix.diagonal_single` (`E_{i,i} = P_i`); `i.val < j.val` is ╬▓-30 upper; `j.val < i.val` is ╬▓-30 lower. Last building block before the spanning theorem (╬▓-31 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AllUnitsAdjoin.lean` |
| `matrix_mem_adjoin` / **`spinS_adjoin_eq_top`** | **­şÄ» Tasaki ┬ğ2.1 Problem 2.1.a (P1d''') general-`S`**: every operator on the `(2S+1)`-dimensional spin-`S` Hilbert space `Ôäé^{N+1}` is a polynomial in `{1╠é, ┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}}`. Equivalently, `Algebra.adjoin Ôäé {┼£^{(1)}, ┼£^{(2)}, ┼£^{(3)}} = Ôèñ`. Proof: every matrix unit `E_{i,j} Ôêê adjoin` (╬▓-31), so by the entry-wise decomposition `M = Ôêæ_{i,j} M_{i,j} ÔÇó E_{i,j}` (`Matrix.matrix_eq_sum_single`) and the linearity of the subalgebra, every matrix is in the adjoin (╬▓-32 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/SpanningTheorem.lean` |
| `ManyBodyOpS` / `onSiteS` / `spinSSiteOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}` | **Multi-site spin-`S` operator space** indexed by configurations `¤â : ╬ø ÔåÆ Fin (N + 1)`, with the site-embedded operator `onSiteS i A` acting as `A` on site `i` and as the identity elsewhere; site-specialised `┼£_i^{(╬▒)}, ┼£_i^┬▒`. | `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_sq` | **Multi-spin Kramers degeneracy at `S = 1/2`** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.3 half-odd-integer extension): `╬İ╠é_tot┬▓ = (-1)^|╬ø| ┬À 1╠é` ÔÇö `+1╠é` when `|╬ø|` is even, `-1╠é` when odd | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_basisVec` | action of `╬İ╠é_tot` on a many-body basis state: `╬İ╠é_tot |╬¿_¤âÔş® = (ÔêÅ_x ╬Á(flip ¤â x)) ┬À |╬¿_{flip ¤â}Ôş®` ÔÇö natural many-body generalisation of `╬İ╠é|ÔåæÔş® = |ÔåôÔş®` and `╬İ╠é|ÔåôÔş® = -|ÔåæÔş®` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |

| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_spinHalfDot_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the bilinear `┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y`** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.3): `╬İ╠é_tot ((┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y) v) = (┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y)(╬İ╠é_tot v)` ÔÇö two equivariance `-1` factors cancel; sums per-axis | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the Heisenberg Hamiltonian** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.3): for real coupling `J` (`conj(J(x,y)) = J(x,y)`), `╬İ╠é_tot ((H J) v) = (H J)(╬İ╠é_tot v)`. ### Multi-body operator space (abstract lattice)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ2.2, pp. 21-26 (tensor-product Hilbert space and site-local
operators). The lattice `╬ø` is an arbitrary finite set with decidable
equality; specializing to `╬ø = Fin N` recovers an `N`-site chain.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `ManyBodyOp ╬ø` | `Matrix (╬ø ÔåÆ Fin 2) (╬ø ÔåÆ Fin 2) Ôäé` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite i A` | site-embedded operator at `i : ╬ø` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_isHermitian` | `A.IsHermitian ÔåÆ (onSite i A).IsHermitian` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_add`, `onSite_sub`, `onSite_zero`, `onSite_smul`, `onSite_one` | linearity of the site embedding and `onSite i 1 = 1` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne` | distinct-site commutation (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x Ôëá y`, S = 1/2) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `basisVec` / `onSite_mulVec_basisVec` | tensor-product basis states and their action under site operators (Tasaki (2.2.1)/(2.2.4)) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_same` | same-site product `onSite i A ┬À onSite i B = onSite i (A ┬À B)` (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x = y`) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_same` | same-site commutator `[onSite i A, onSite i B] = onSite i [A, B]` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.mul_of_commute` | commuting Hermitians multiply Hermitian | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |

| `marshallSignOf_im_eq_zero` | the Marshall sign `marshallSignOf A ¤â` is **real**: `(marshallSignOf A ¤â).im = 0`. | `dot_marshallDressed_heisenbergHamiltonian_marshallDressed_im_eq_zero` | **MLM Property (i)**: for real coupling `J`, the dressed Heisenberg bilinear pairing `╬ú_¤ä \|╬¿╠â^¤âÔş® ¤ä ┬À (H ┬À \|╬¿╠â^{¤â'}Ôş®) ¤ä` is real (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5, p. 41 in the proof of Theorem 2.2). | `marshallSignOf_mul_marshallSignOf_basisSwap_of_bipartite_antiparallel` | **Marshall sign relation**: for a bond `{x, y}` crossing the bipartition (`A x Ôëá A y`) with `¤â` antiparallel at `{x, y}` (`¤â x Ôëá ¤â y`), `marshallSignOf A ¤â * marshallSignOf A (basisSwap ¤â x y) = -1`. The combined product over `╬ø` of pairwise factors collapses: outside `{x, y}` each pairwise factor is `(┬▒1)┬▓ = 1`; at the unique site in `A Ôê® {x, y}` the pair contributes `(-1)^(¤â x + ¤â y) = -1` since `¤â x Ôëá ¤â y`; the other site of `{x, y}` lies outside `A` and contributes `1` | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/MarshallSignTrick.lean` |

| `sublatticeSpinSquaredS_commute_totalSpinSOpPlus` / `_totalSpinSOpMinus` / `bipartiteToyGroundStateSubspacePredicted_totalSpinSOpPlus_invariant` / `_totalSpinSOpMinus_invariant` | **┼£^+_tot / ┼£^-_tot-invariance of the predicted GS subspace**: derived commutations `[(┼£_A)┬▓, ┼£^┬▒_tot] = 0` via the Cartesian commutations + `totalSpinSOp{Plus,Minus}_eq_add/sub`, plus the predicted-GS invariance under each ladder operator via the same pattern as PR #2798. Combined with PRs #2798 / #2799, full `su(2)` algebra closure: predicted GS is invariant under Cartan {┼£^z_tot} and ladders {┼£^+_tot, ┼£^-_tot}, hence under the entire `su(2)` Lie algebra generated by these (PR #2800, file `Quantum/SpinS/BipartiteToyGSLadderInvariant.lean`) |

| `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_cross_commute` | the two sublattice Casimirs commute: `Commute (┼£_A)┬▓ (┼£_┬¼A)┬▓`. Each pairwise component `Commute ((┼£_A^(╬▒))┬▓) ((┼£_┬¼A^(╬▓))┬▓)` follows from the mixed-axes cross-commute by chaining `Commute.mul_left` / `mul_right`. Sets up the joint eigenbasis of `(┼£_tot)┬▓`, `(┼£_A)┬▓`, `(┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` for the toy-Hamiltonian eigenvalue analysis | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpin.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}_commutator_sublatticeSpinHalfOp{2,3,1}` | **Sublattice SU(2) algebra**: `[┼£_A^(╬▒), ┼£_A^(╬▓)] = i ╬Á^╬▒╬▓╬│ ┼£_A^(╬│)` for each cyclic axis triple. Generic helper `sublatticeSpin_commutator_general` lifts the single-site commutator `[S╬▒, S╬▓] = i ÔÇó S╬│` to the sublattice sum (off-diagonal pairs vanish by `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne`; diagonal contributes `if A x then i ÔÇó onSite x S╬│ else 0`) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpin.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_commute_sublatticeSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` | **Sublattice Casimir self-invariance**: `Commute (┼£_A)┬▓ (┼£_A^(╬▒))` for each axis. Standard SU(2) Casimir argument applied at the sublattice level: per-axis Leibniz rule `[X┬▓, C] = X[X,C] + [X,C]X` combined with the sublattice SU(2) algebra. Together with cross-commute, gives `Commute (┼£_A)┬▓ (┼£_tot^(╬▒))`, hence `Commute (┼£_A)┬▓ (┼£_tot)┬▓` | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpin.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_commute_sublatticeSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}_complement` / `_totalSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}` / `_totalSpinHalfSquared` | `(┼£_A)┬▓` commutes with each `┼£_┬¼A^(╬▒)` (`Commute.mul_left` over the mixed-axes cross-commute), with each `┼£_tot^(╬▒) = ┼£_A^(╬▒) + ┼£_┬¼A^(╬▒)`, and with `(┼£_tot)┬▓ = ╬ú_╬▒ (┼£_tot^(╬▒))┬▓`. Provides the **third pairwise commutativity** needed for the joint eigenbasis of `(┼£_tot)┬▓`, `(┼£_A)┬▓`, `(┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` (the first two are ╬▒-6r self-invariance and ╬▒-6o inter-Casimir cross-commute) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpin.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinDot` / `sublatticeSpinDot_complement_isHermitian` | cross-sublattice spin dot product: `┼£_A ┬À ┼£_B := ╬ú_╬▒ ┼£_A^(╬▒) ┼£_B^(╬▒)`. `┼£_A ┬À ┼£_┬¼A` is Hermitian (each summand is the product of two commuting Hermitian operators). Bilinear expansion `sublatticeSpinDot_eq_sum_sum`: `┼£_A ┬À ┼£_B = ╬ú_{x : A x} ╬ú_{y : B y} ┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y` connects the operator-level Casimir form to the bond-level Heisenberg expression in the toy Hamiltonian (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.10)) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpinDot.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_eq_sum_dot` / `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_basisVec_const` / `_all_up` / `_all_down` / `_of_const_on` | `(┼£_A)┬▓ = ╬ú_{x Ôêê A} ╬ú_{y Ôêê A} ┼£_x ┬À ┼£_y` (specialisation `B = A` of the bilinear expansion), and the **maximum-spin Casimir eigenvalue on the all-aligned state**: `(┼£_A)┬▓ ┬À \|s s ÔÇĞ sÔş® = (\|A\|┬À(\|A\|+2)/4) ┬À \|s s ÔÇĞ sÔş®` for any `s : Fin 2`. Generalised form `_of_const_on`: any `\|¤âÔş®` with `¤â` **constant on `A`** is an eigenvector with eigenvalue `\|A\|┬À(\|A\|+2)/4` (relevant for N├®el-style states which are constant on each sublattice but not globally) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeSpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_eq_sublatticeSpinDot_sum` | the MLM toy Hamiltonian decomposes as an oriented cross-sublattice spin dot product: `─ñ_toy = ┼£_A ┬À ┼£_┬¼A + ┼£_┬¼A ┬À ┼£_A`. Bridges the bipartite-bond sum (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.10)) to the operator-level Casimir form (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.11)) | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinDot_complement_comm` / `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_eq_two_sublatticeSpinDot` | cross-sublattice symmetry: `┼£_A ┬À ┼£_┬¼A = ┼£_┬¼A ┬À ┼£_A` (each axis pair commutes by `sublatticeSpinHalfOp{1,2,3}_cross_commute`), giving the closed form `─ñ_toy = 2 ÔÇó ┼£_A ┬À ┼£_┬¼A` | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_eq_sublattice_casimir` / `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_eq_casimir_diff` | **Casimir identity** (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 (2.5.11)): `(┼£_tot)┬▓ = (┼£_A)┬▓ + 2 ÔÇó (┼£_A ┬À ┼£_┬¼A) + (┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` (per-axis `(a + b)┬▓ = a┬▓ + 2ab + b┬▓` via cross-commute), and the closed form (without `1/|╬ø|`) `─ñ_toy = (┼£_tot)┬▓ ÔêÆ (┼£_A)┬▓ ÔêÆ (┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfSquared` | the toy Hamiltonian commutes with `(┼£_tot)┬▓` (specialisation of `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfSquared`). The standard fact used to project the toy ground state onto a fixed `(┼£_tot)┬▓` eigenspace, underpinning the `S_tot = 0` selection of the toy ground state | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_commute_sublatticeSpinHalfSquared` / `_complement` | the toy Hamiltonian commutes with `(┼£_A)┬▓` and with `(┼£_┬¼A)┬▓`. Direct consequences of the closed form `─ñ_toy = (┼£_tot)┬▓ ÔêÆ (┼£_A)┬▓ ÔêÆ (┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` and the three pairwise Casimir commutativities (PRs ╬▒-6o, ╬▒-6s, self-commute trivially). Together with ╬▒-6p, gives all four Casimir-style commutators of `─ñ_toy`, the prerequisite for the joint eigenbasis analysis on which the `S_tot = 0` selection rests | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `heisenbergToyHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_const` / `_simplified` | explicit eigenvalue of `─ñ_toy` on the all-aligned state: the Casimir-difference form `\|╬ø\|┬À(\|╬ø\|+2)/4 ÔêÆ \|A\|┬À(\|A\|+2)/4 ÔêÆ \|┬¼A\|┬À(\|┬¼A\|+2)/4` algebraically simplifies via `\|╬ø\| = \|A\| + \|┬¼A\|` to the **product form** `\|A\|┬À\|┬¼A\|/2`. The eigenvalue is non-negative for any bipartite lattice and strictly positive when both sublattices are non-empty | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/ToyHamiltonianCasimir.lean` |
| `sublatticeSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_neelStateOf` / `_complement_mulVec_neelStateOf` | sublattice Casimir eigenvalues on the **N├®el state** `╬Ğ_N├®el(A) := basisVec (neelConfigOf A)`: `(┼£_A)┬▓ ┬À \|╬Ğ_N├®el(A)Ôş® = (\|A\|┬À(\|A\|+2)/4) ┬À \|╬Ğ_N├®el(A)Ôş®` and `(┼£_┬¼A)┬▓ ┬À \|╬Ğ_N├®el(A)Ôş® = (\|┬¼A\|┬À(\|┬¼A\|+2)/4) ┬À \|╬Ğ_N├®el(A)Ôş®`. Direct corollaries of `_of_const_on` since the N├®el configuration is constant on each sublattice (`¤â x = 0` on `A`, `¤â x = 1` on `┬¼A`); the N├®el state is simultaneously a `(┼£_A)┬▓` and `(┼£_┬¼A)┬▓` eigenvector at maximum-spin eigenvalues | `Quantum/MarshallLiebMattis/SublatticeCasimirNeel.lean` |
| `mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_commute_of_mem` | generic preservation: any operator `A` with `Commute A (┼£tot^(3))` maps each magnetisation sector `H_M` to itself ÔÇö operator-level form of Tasaki ┬ğ2.2 (2.2.10), p. 22 block-diagonalisation | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | Casimir specialisation: `┼£tot┬▓` preserves every `H_M` (since `[┼£tot┬▓, ┼£tot^(3)] = 0`) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | for any `J : ╬ø ÔåÆ ╬ø ÔåÆ Ôäé` and `M : Ôäé`, `v Ôêê H_M` implies `H ┬À v Ôêê H_M` ÔÇö the operator-level statement that any Heisenberg Hamiltonian block-diagonalises against Tasaki ┬ğ2.2 (2.2.10), p. 22 magnetisation-sector decomposition (consequence of SU(2) invariance `[H, ┼£tot^(3)] = 0`) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfOpMinus_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | for any `M : Ôäé`, `v Ôêê H_M` implies `┼£tot^- ┬À v Ôêê H_{M-1}` ÔÇö the standard SU(2) lowering ladder action via the Cartan relation `[┼£tot^(3), ┼£tot^-] = -┼£tot^-` | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |

| `onSite_exp_eq_exp_onSite` | `onSite x (exp A) = exp (onSite x A)` ÔÇö bridge between single-site and many-body matrix exponential. Local Frobenius normed structure + `LinearMap.continuous_of_finiteDimensional` + `NormedSpace.map_exp` | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |

### Two-site spin inner product (Tasaki ┬ğ2.2 eq. (2.2.16))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ2.2 eq. (2.2.16), p. 24.

| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_basisVec_const` | `H ┬À (┼£_tot^+ ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®) = c_J ┬À (┼£_tot^+ ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®)` ÔÇö `┼£_tot^+` preserves the H-eigenvalue on a constant-spin basis state (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_basisVec_const` | same with `┼£_tot^-` ÔÇö the canonical lowering ladder Tasaki uses to enumerate the ferromagnetic ground states `|╬Ğ_MÔş®` (eq. (2.4.9), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_pow_basisVec_const` | iterated form: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : Ôäò`, `H ┬À ((┼£_tot^-)^k ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®) = c_J ┬À ((┼£_tot^-)^k ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®)`; specialised at `s = 0` this gives the unnormalised Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.9), p. 33 ÔÇö every iterate `(┼£_tot^-)^k ┬À |╬ĞÔåæÔş®` lies in the same H-eigenspace as `|╬ĞÔåæÔş®` | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_pow_basisVec_const` | companion iterated form for `┼£_tot^+`: for any constant `s : Fin 2` and any `k : Ôäò`, `H ┬À ((┼£_tot^+)^k ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®) = c_J ┬À ((┼£_tot^+)^k ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®)` (corollary of SU(2) invariance, Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.7), iterated) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_commute_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}` | for any `J` and `╬© : ÔäØ`, `H` commutes with the global rotation `├ø^(╬▒)_╬© = exp(-i╬© ┼£_tot^╬▒)` (composes `heisenbergHamiltonian_commutator_totalSpinHalfOp{╬▒}` with `totalSpinHalfRot{╬▒}_commute_of_commute`; the operator-level form of Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `╬©`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ┬À (├ø^(╬▒)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®) = c_J ┬À (├ø^(╬▒)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®)` ÔÇö the rotated (single-axis) constant-spin state shares the H-eigenvalue (Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfRot32_basisVec_const` | for any `J`, `╬©`, `¤ò`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H ┬À (├ø^(3)_¤ò ┬À ├ø^(2)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®) = c_J ┬À (├ø^(3)_¤ò ┬À ├ø^(2)_╬© ┬À |sÔÇĞsÔş®)` ÔÇö the two-step spin-coherent state of Tasaki eq. (2.4.6) (`|╬Ş_╬©,¤òÔş®` for `s = 0`) is an H-eigenvector with the same eigenvalue as the constant configuration (Tasaki eq. (2.4.7), p. 33) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | `┼£_tot┬▓ (|ÔåæÔåôÔş® - |ÔåôÔåæÔş®) = 0` for `╬ø = Fin 2` (singlet, `S = 0`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfSquared_mulVec_two_site_triplet_zero` | `┼£_tot┬▓ (|ÔåæÔåôÔş® + |ÔåôÔåæÔş®) = 2(|ÔåæÔåôÔş® + |ÔåôÔåæÔş®)` for `╬ø = Fin 2` (triplet `m = 0`, `S = 1`) | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfOp3_mulVec_two_site_singlet` | the two-site singlet has zero `┼£_tot^(3)` magnetization | `Quantum/SpinDot.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_totalOnSite` | `[onSite x S╬▒, ╬ú_z onSite z S╬▓] = onSite x [S╬▒, S╬▓]` | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |

### One-dimensional open-chain quantum Ising

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ3.3 eq. (3.3.1), p. 55 (transverse-field Ising on an open
chain). Our formalization uses the Pauli convention `¤â = 2┬ÀS` and an
explicit bond coupling `J`.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h` | `H = -J ╬ú ¤â^z_i ¤â^z_{i+1} - h ╬ú ¤â^x_i` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_isHermitian` | `H` is Hermitian for real `J`, `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot x y` | the Ising bond operator `¤â^z_x ┬À ¤â^z_y` (generic in `╬ø`) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot_isHermitian` | each bond operator is Hermitian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric (J : ╬ø ÔåÆ ╬ø ÔåÆ Ôäé) (h : Ôäé)` | **graph-friendly** Ising Hamiltonian `╬ú J(x,y) ¤â^z_x ¤â^z_y ÔêÆ h ╬ú ¤â^x_x` for any finite `╬ø` and pairwise coupling `J`; specialises to chain / graph / lattice via the choice of `J` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric_isHermitian` | Hermitian for entry-wise real `J` and real `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph G J h` | graph wrapper: `isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf G J) h`; double-sum convention matches Heisenberg-on-graph | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph_isHermitian` | Hermitian for real `J, h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph G ╬▓ J h` | Gibbs state of the graph-built Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_isHermitian` / `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_commute_hamiltonian` | Hermiticity (real `J, h`) and commute with the Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.sum_pathGraph_forward` / `sum_pathGraph_backward` / `sum_pathGraph_adj` | sum-decomposition helpers for `pathGraph (N+1)` adjacency: `╬ú_{x,y}` over ordered adjacent pairs = `╬ú_{i:Fin N} (f i.cs i.s + f i.s i.cs)` | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `pathGraphParityColoring` / `pathGraph_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of `pathGraph (N + 1)` (`i ÔåĞ i.val % 2`) and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Underpins the N├®el state (`Quantum/NeelState.lean`) and the Marshall-Lieb-Mattis theorem (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `cycleGraphEvenParityColoring` / `cycleGraph_even_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of the even cycle `cycleGraph (2 * K + 2)` and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Wrap-around case `(2K+1) + 1 Ôëí 0` still flips parity because the cycle length is even (odd cycles are not bipartite) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_eq_isingHamiltonianGeneric` | **generic-N bridge**: `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h = isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf (pathGraph (N+1)) (-J/2)) h`. The proof itself is the robust regression test | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_mul_hamiltonian_im` | for Hermitian `O`, `(Ôş¿H_Ising ┬À OÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_anticommutator_im` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(Ôş¿A┬ÀB + B┬ÀAÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_commutator_re` | for Hermitian `A, B`, `(Ôş¿A┬ÀB ÔêÆ B┬ÀAÔş®_╬▓).re = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsHamiltonianVariance_im` | `(Var_╬▓(H_Ising)).im = 0` (energy variance real) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsing_partitionFn_im` | `(partitionFn ╬▓ H_Ising).im = 0` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_ofReal_re_eq` | for Hermitian `O`, `((Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓).re : Ôäé) = Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(¤ü_╬▓^n) = Z(n╬▓) / Z(╬▓)^n` for the Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `quantumIsingGibbsExpectation_self_eq` | `Ôş¿H_IsingÔş®_╬▓ = -J ┬À Ôêæ Ôş¿¤â^z ¤â^zÔş®_╬▓ + (-h) ┬À Ôêæ Ôş¿¤â^xÔş®_╬▓` (energy as bond + transverse-field decomposition) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

### Gibbs state (Tasaki ┬ğ3.3)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ3.3.

All theorems in this module are fully proved with **zero `sorry`**.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `gibbsExp ╬▓ H` | `exp(-╬▓H) := Matrix.exp (-╬▓ ÔÇó H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isHermitian` | `exp(-╬▓H)` is Hermitian (when `H` is Hermitian) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_zero` | `exp(-0┬ÀH) = 1` (Tasaki ┬ğ3.3, pp. 75ÔÇô78) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add` | `exp(-(╬▓Ôéü+╬▓Ôéé)H) = exp(-╬▓ÔéüH) ┬À exp(-╬▓ÔééH)` (one-parameter group) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add_of_commute_hamiltonians` | `exp(-╬▓(HÔéü+HÔéé)) = exp(-╬▓HÔéü) ┬À exp(-╬▓HÔéé)` for commuting `HÔéü, HÔéé` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_neg_mul_self` | `exp(╬▓H) ┬À exp(-╬▓H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_self_mul_neg` | `exp(-╬▓H) ┬À exp(╬▓H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isUnit` | `exp(-╬▓H)` is invertible | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_ne_zero` | `exp(-╬▓H) Ôëá 0` (corollary of `gibbsExp_isUnit`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_ne_zero` | `¤ü_╬▓ Ôëá 0` when `Z(╬▓) Ôëá 0` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_inv` | `(¤ü_╬▓)Ôü╗┬╣ = Z(╬▓) ┬À e^{╬▓H}` when `Z(╬▓) Ôëá 0` (general matrix inverse, generalises `gibbsState_zero_inv`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_smul_gibbsState_eq_gibbsExp` | `Z(╬▓) ┬À ¤ü_╬▓ = e^{-╬▓H}` when `Z(╬▓) Ôëá 0` (canonical rescaled identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_mul_gibbsExpectation_eq` | `Z(╬▓) ┬À Ôş¿AÔş®_╬▓ = Tr(e^{-╬▓H} ┬À A)` when `Z(╬▓) Ôëá 0` (canonical unnormalised expectation) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_natCast_mul` | `exp(-(n┬À╬▓)H) = (exp(-╬▓H))^n` for `n : Ôäò` (exact discrete semigroup identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_two_mul` | `exp(-(2╬▓)H) = exp(-╬▓H) ┬À exp(-╬▓H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_inv` | `(exp(-╬▓H))Ôü╗┬╣ = exp(╬▓H)` (matrix inverse made explicit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_intCast_mul` | `exp(-(n┬À╬▓)H) = (exp(-╬▓H))^n` for `n : Ôäñ` (integer-power extension) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn ╬▓ H` | `Z := Matrix.trace (exp(-╬▓H))` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_zero` | `Z(0) = Fintype.card (╬ø ÔåÆ Fin 2)` (dimension of the Hilbert space) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_zero_ne_zero` | `Z(0) Ôëá 0` (concrete sorry-free proof that the partition function is nonzero at ╬▓ = 0) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.trace_im` | for any Hermitian `A : Matrix n n Ôäé`, `A.trace.im = 0` (generic helper) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `partitionFn_im_of_isHermitian` | for Hermitian `H`, `(partitionFn ╬▓ H).im = 0` (Z is real) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_mul_self_trace` | `Tr(¤ü_╬▓┬▓) = Z(2╬▓) / Z(╬▓)┬▓` (purity / R├®nyi-2 entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_pow_trace` | `Tr(¤ü_╬▓^n) = Z(n╬▓) / Z(╬▓)^n` for any `n : Ôäò` (R├®nyi-n entropy precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_zero` | `¤ü_0 = (1/dim) ┬À I` (maximally mixed state at infinite temperature) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_zero_inv` | `¤ü_0Ôü╗┬╣ = dim ┬À I` (matrix inverse at ╬▓ = 0) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_zero` | `Ôş¿AÔş®_0 = (1/dim) ┬À Tr A` (high-temperature limit) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState ╬▓ H` | `¤ü := (1/Z) ÔÇó exp(-╬▓H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_trace` | `Tr(¤ü) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_isHermitian` | `¤ü` is Hermitian | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation ╬▓ H O` | `Ôş¿OÔş® := Matrix.trace (¤ü * O)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_one` | `Ôş¿1Ôş® = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_add` | `Ôş¿OÔéü + OÔééÔş® = Ôş¿OÔéüÔş® + Ôş¿OÔééÔş®` (linearity in observable) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_smul` | `Ôş¿c ┬À OÔş® = c ┬À Ôş¿OÔş®` (scalar linearity, `c : Ôäé`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_neg` | `Ôş¿-OÔş® = -Ôş¿OÔş®` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sub` | `Ôş¿A - BÔş® = Ôş¿AÔş® - Ôş¿BÔş®` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sum` | `Ôş¿Ôêæ i Ôêê s, f iÔş® = Ôêæ i Ôêê s, Ôş¿f iÔş®` (finite-sum linearity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_commute_hamiltonian` | `[exp(-╬▓H), H] = 0` (Tasaki ┬ğ3.3, p. 80) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_commute_hamiltonian` | `[¤ü_╬▓, H] = 0`, i.e. `¤ü_╬▓` is stationary under the dynamics generated by `H` (Tasaki ┬ğ3.3, p. 80) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `Matrix.trace_mul_star_of_isHermitian` | `star (Tr(A ┬À B)) = Tr(A ┬À B)` for Hermitian `A, B : Matrix n n Ôäé` (algebraic core, Gibbs-independent) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_star_of_isHermitian` | `star Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓ = Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓` for Hermitian `H`, `O` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_im_of_isHermitian` | `(Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` for Hermitian `H`, `O` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_ofReal_re_eq_of_isHermitian` | `((Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓).re : Ôäé) = Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓` for Hermitian `H`, `O` (real-cast equality) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_mul_hamiltonian_comm` | `Ôş¿H ┬À AÔş®_╬▓ = Ôş¿A ┬À HÔş®_╬▓` for any `A` (Tasaki ┬ğ3.3, p. 80) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_mul_comm_of_commute_hamiltonian` | for any conserved `A` (`[A, H] = 0`), `Ôş¿A ┬À OÔş®_╬▓ = Ôş¿O ┬À AÔş®_╬▓` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_commutator_eq_zero_of_commute_hamiltonian` | for any conserved `A`, `Ôş¿A ┬À O ÔêÆ O ┬À AÔş®_╬▓ = 0` (selection rule) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_commutator_hamiltonian` | `Ôş¿[H, A]Ôş®_╬▓ = 0` (conservation law) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_hamiltonian_im` | `(Ôş¿HÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` for Hermitian `H` (real energy expectation) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_sq_im_of_isHermitian` | `(Ôş¿O ┬À OÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` for Hermitian `H, O` (second-moment realness, variance precursor) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExpectation_pow_im_of_isHermitian` | `(Ôş¿O^nÔş®_╬▓).im = 0` for Hermitian `H, O`, any `n : Ôäò` (all natural-power moments real) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance ╬▓ H O` | `Var_╬▓(O) := Ôş¿O ┬À OÔş®_╬▓ ÔêÆ Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓┬▓` (canonical-ensemble variance) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_eq` | unfolding lemma for `gibbsVariance` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_im_of_isHermitian` | `(Var_╬▓(O)).im = 0` for Hermitian `H, O` (variance is real) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_zero` | at ╬▓ = 0, `Var_0(O) = (1/dim) ┬À Tr(O┬▓) ÔêÆ ((1/dim) ┬À Tr O)┬▓` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_eq_centered_sq` | `Var_╬▓(O) = Ôş¿(O ÔêÆ Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓ ┬À 1) ┬À (O ÔêÆ Ôş¿OÔş®_╬▓ ┬À 1)Ôş®_╬▓` (centered-square form, `Z Ôëá 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance ╬▓ H A B` | `Cov_╬▓(A, B) := Ôş¿A ┬À BÔş®_╬▓ ÔêÆ Ôş¿AÔş®_╬▓ ┬À Ôş¿BÔş®_╬▓` (canonical-ensemble complex covariance) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_eq` | unfolding lemma for `gibbsCovariance` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_self_eq_variance` | `Cov_╬▓(O, O) = Var_╬▓(O)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_sub_swap_eq_commutator` | `Cov_╬▓(A, B) ÔêÆ Cov_╬▓(B, A) = Ôş¿A ┬À B ÔêÆ B ┬À AÔş®_╬▓` (antisymmetric part = commutator expectation) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_add_left` | `Cov_╬▓(AÔéü + AÔéé, B) = Cov_╬▓(AÔéü, B) + Cov_╬▓(AÔéé, B)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_add_right` | `Cov_╬▓(A, BÔéü + BÔéé) = Cov_╬▓(A, BÔéü) + Cov_╬▓(A, BÔéé)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_smul_left` | `Cov_╬▓(c ÔÇó A, B) = c ┬À Cov_╬▓(A, B)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_smul_right` | `Cov_╬▓(A, c ÔÇó B) = c ┬À Cov_╬▓(A, B)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovariance_const_smul_one_left/right_eq_zero` | `Cov_╬▓(c ÔÇó 1, B) = 0` and `Cov_╬▓(A, c ÔÇó 1) = 0` (when `Z Ôëá 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_const_smul_one_left/right_eq_zero` | `Cov^s_╬▓(c ÔÇó 1, B) = 0` and `Cov^s_╬▓(A, c ÔÇó 1) = 0` (when `Z Ôëá 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm ╬▓ H A B` | `Cov^s_╬▓(A, B) := (1/2) ┬À Ôş¿A ┬À B + B ┬À AÔş®_╬▓ ÔêÆ Ôş¿AÔş®_╬▓ ┬À Ôş¿BÔş®_╬▓` (symmetric / real-valued covariance) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_self_eq_variance` | `Cov^s_╬▓(O, O) = Var_╬▓(O)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_comm` | `Cov^s_╬▓(A, B) = Cov^s_╬▓(B, A)` (symmetric in observables) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_add_left/right` | additivity of `Cov^s_╬▓` in each argument | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_smul_left/right` | scalar pull-out from each argument of `Cov^s_╬▓` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_add` | `Var_╬▓(A + B) = Var_╬▓(A) + Var_╬▓(B) + 2 ┬À Cov^s_╬▓(A, B)` (sum-of-observables variance identity) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_one` | `Var_╬▓(1) = 0` (when `Z Ôëá 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_smul` | `Var_╬▓(c ÔÇó A) = c┬▓ ┬À Var_╬▓(A)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_smul_one` | `Var_╬▓(c ÔÇó 1) = 0` (when `Z Ôëá 0`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsVariance_neg` | `Var_╬▓(ÔêÆA) = Var_╬▓(A)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

| `gibbsCovariance_eq_symm_add_half_commutator` | `Cov_╬▓(A, B) = Cov^s_╬▓(A, B) + (1/2) ┬À Ôş¿A ┬À B ÔêÆ B ┬À AÔş®_╬▓` (symmetric / antisymmetric decomposition) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsCovarianceSymm_eq_half_add_swap` | `Cov^s_╬▓(A, B) = (1/2) ┬À (Cov_╬▓(A, B) + Cov_╬▓(B, A))` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

### Heisenberg chain (Tasaki ┬ğ3.5)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, ┬ğ3.5, p. 89.

| Lean name | Statement | File |

| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf G J` | the canonical pairwise coupling `╬ø ÔåÆ ╬ø ÔåÆ Ôäé` of a `SimpleGraph G` with uniform edge weight `J`: returns `J` on edges of `G`, zero otherwise (graph-centric bridge) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.couplingOf_symm` / `_self` / `_real` | symmetry (from `G.Adj` symmetry), vanishing on the diagonal (from irreflexivity), and reality (for real edge weight) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |

| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_all_down` | `H_open(N=1) ┬À |ÔåôÔåôÔş® = -(J/2) ┬À |ÔåôÔåôÔş®` ÔÇö all-down state has the same eigenvalue as all-up (both are `S = 1` triplet states) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_two_site_mulVec_basisVec_triplet_zero` | `H_open(N=1) ┬À (|ÔåæÔåôÔş® + |ÔåôÔåæÔş®) = -(J/2) ┬À (|ÔåæÔåôÔş® + |ÔåôÔåæÔş®)` ÔÇö triplet `m = 0` state, completing the 3-fold degenerate triplet representation `S = 1` with eigenvalue `-J/2` | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_three_site_eq` | for `N = 2` (the 3-site open chain on `Fin 3`, 2 bonds), `H_open = -2J ┬À (spinHalfDot 0 1 + spinHalfDot 1 2)` ÔÇö explicit two-bond reduction | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_three_site_mulVec_basisVec_all_up` | `H_open(N=2) ┬À |ÔåæÔåæÔåæÔş® = -J ┬À |ÔåæÔåæÔåæÔş®` ÔÇö confirming the linear scaling `E(|Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş®) = -N┬ÀJ/2` (here `N = 2` bonds, `J = 1` per bond) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainCoupling_sum_eq` | for any `N : Ôäò`, `╬ú_{x,y Ôêê Fin (N+1)} openChainCoupling N J x y = -(2N ┬À J : Ôäé)` (the bond-counting lemma: each of the `N` unordered nearest-neighbour bonds is counted in both orientations) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_const` | for any `N : Ôäò`, `J : ÔäØ`, and constant `s : Fin 2`, `H_open ┬À |s..sÔş® = -(N┬ÀJ/2 : Ôäé) ┬À |s..sÔş®` ÔÇö both `s = 0` (all-up) and `s = 1` (all-down) share the same eigenvalue by SU(2) symmetry | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_up` | `s = 0` specialisation of the above (Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.5)/(2.4.1) ferromagnetic ground-state energy `E_GS = -|B|┬ÀS┬▓` for `S = 1/2`, `|B| = N` bonds) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_basisVec_all_down` | `s = 1` specialisation: same eigenvalue `-(N┬ÀJ/2)` for the all-down state by SU(2) symmetry | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpMinus_pow_basisVec_all_up` | for any `N : Ôäò`, `J : ÔäØ`, `k : Ôäò`, `H_open ┬À ((┼£tot^-)^k ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş®) = -(N┬ÀJ/2 : Ôäé) ┬À ((┼£tot^-)^k ┬À |Ôåæ..ÔåæÔş®)` ÔÇö the unnormalised Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 (2.4.9) ferromagnetic ground states `|╬Ğ_MÔş®` made explicit on the chain (combines PRs #82 + #98) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_totalSpinHalfOpPlus_pow_basisVec_all_down` | dual ladder from `|Ôåô..ÔåôÔş®`, same eigenvalue `-(N┬ÀJ/2)` | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `openChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | `H_open` preserves every magnetisation subspace `H_M` (chain specialisation of PR #91) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `periodicChainHeisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace_of_mem` | `H_periodic` preserves every magnetisation subspace `H_M` (chain specialisation of PR #91) | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |

### Perron-Frobenius theorem (`Math/PerronFrobenius.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean`, `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean`)

Perron-Frobenius theorem for nonneg irreducible/primitive matrices (Issue #405, closed).
The sorry in `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` is eliminated via the Collatz-Wielandt port (PRs AÔÇôC).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `Matrix.IsPrimitive.of_irreducible_pos_diagonal` | irreducible nonneg + positive diagonal ÔåÆ primitive (Seneta ┬ğ1.1, Prop. 1.3, p. 17) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.collatzWielandtFn` | CW function `min_{i\|x_i>0} (Ax)_i/x_i` (Seneta ┬ğ1.2, p. 27) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_any_ratio` | `CW(x) Ôëñ (Ax)_i/x_i` for `x_i > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.le_mulVec` | fundamental inequality `CW(x)┬Àx Ôëñ Ax` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.smul_eq` | scale invariance `CW(cx) = CW(x)` for `c > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.upperSemicontinuousOn` | CW is upper-semicontinuous on stdSimplex | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.exists_maximizer` | CW attains its max on stdSimplex (EVT for USC, Seneta ┬ğ1.2, p. 28) | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.eq_eigenvalue` | `CW(v) = r` when `Av = r┬Àv`, `v > 0` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `CollatzWielandt.lt_of_all_ratios_gt` | all ratios `> c` Ôş╣ `CW(x) > c` | `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.pos_of_nonneg_eigenvec` | irreducible nonneg + `Av = ╬╝v`, `v ÔëÑ 0`, `v Ôëá 0` Ôş╣ `v > 0` (standard propagation argument) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_primitive` | primitive nonneg Ôş╣ Ôêâ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ┬ğ1.2, pp. 27ÔÇô28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `PerronFrobeniusMain.exists_positive_eigenvector_of_irreducible` | irreducible nonneg Ôş╣ Ôêâ `r > 0`, `v > 0` with `Av = rv` (Seneta ┬ğ1.2, pp. 27ÔÇô28) | `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean` |
| `exists_nonneg_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry**, retained for docs) symmetric nonneg max eigenvalue has nonneg eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `exists_pos_eigenvec_max` | (**sorry-free**) irreducible nonneg Hermitian Ôş╣ max eigenvalue has strictly positive eigenvector | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique` | strictly positive eigenvector unique up to positive scalar | `Math/PerronFrobenius.lean` |

References: E. Seneta, *Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006, ┬ğ1.2 (pp. 27ÔÇô28);
or4nge19/MCMC: `MCMC/PF/LinearAlgebra/Matrix/PerronFrobenius/`.

### Spin-`S` MarshallÔÇôLiebÔÇôMattis on the magnetization sector (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 generic S, sector form)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 applied to the
**magnetization-`M` sector** of the un-dressed antiferromagnetic
Heisenberg Hamiltonian on a bipartite graph. The sector subtype
`magConfigS V N M := { ¤â : V ÔåÆ Fin (N + 1) // magSumS ¤â = M }` is the
natural index type since the dressed Heisenberg matrix is irreducible
on each sector. The core sector-matrix API lives in
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSector.lean`; the trailing
eigenvalue-uniqueness + complex-form MLM Theorem 2.2 statements
were moved to the companion
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSectorEigenvalueUnique.lean` in
refactor #30 (PR #2829). Tracked in Issue #412.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `magConfigS V N M` | sector subtype of magnetization-`M` configurations (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `RaiseLowerStepSMagSector G ¤â ¤ä` / `RaiseLowerReachableSMagSector G` | bipartite raise/lower step lifted to `magConfigS` and its reflexive transitive closure (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `raiseLowerReachableSMagSector_bipartiteCompleteGraph` | any two configurations in the same sector are reachable via raise/lower steps under the bipartite-intermediate hypothesis (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Property (iii) generic-S form) |
| `shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N c M` | shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `c┬À1 - dressed_re` restricted to the sector via `Matrix.submatrix Subtype.val Subtype.val`, the input to PF irreducibility |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N M` | dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg COMPLEX matrix restricted to the sector |
| `isIrreducible_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | `Matrix.IsIrreducible` for the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 ╬│-3 final, MLM PF input) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector existence for the shifted sector matrix (`r > 0`, `v > 0` componentwise) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector uniqueness on the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 nondegeneracy) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF on the dressed sector matrix at eigenvalue `c - r` (Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 dressed-form ground state) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #856) |
| `pos_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector positive eigenvectors share the same eigenvalue (Rayleigh identity for symmetric matrices, PR #856) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_heisenberg` / `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_dressed` | matrix relations `dressed = sign┬Àsign┬Àheis` and inverse via `sign┬▓ = 1` (PR #853) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_dressed_eigenvec` | Marshall sign conjugation of dressed sector eigenvector to un-dressed Heisenberg sector eigenvector (PR #853) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_heis_eigenvec` | inverse Marshall conjugation (PR #854) |
| `exists_marshallSign_eigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector ground-state existence with Marshall sign structure (PR #853) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #854) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvalue uniqueness (PR #856) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState` | bundled Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 (existence + same-eigenvalue uniqueness, PR #855) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2: existence + forced eigenvalue uniqueness + eigenvector uniqueness (PR #859) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_isHermitian` | complex sector matrix is Hermitian for real coupling (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_apply_eq_ofReal` | for real coupling, complex sector entries equal real-form entries embedded in `Ôäé` (PR #857) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_ofReal` | real ÔåÆ complex eigenvector lift (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_re_of_complex_eigenvec` | complex ÔåÆ real real-part extraction (PR #861) |
| `exists_marshallSign_complexEigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 ground-state existence on the un-dressed quantum Heisenberg sector matrix (PR #860) |
| `marshallPositive_complexEigenvec_re_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Marshall-positive uniqueness via real-part extraction (PR #862) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 on the complex sector matrix (PR #863) |

The complex-form `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full`
is the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the
magnetization sector: the ground state of the un-dressed quantum
Heisenberg Hamiltonian restricted to the sector is unique (up to a
positive real scalar in its real part) and has the Marshall sign
structure `╬Ğ ¤â := ((sign A ¤â.1).re * v ¤â : Ôäé)` with `v > 0`.

References: H. Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, Springer 2020, ┬ğ2.5 Theorem 2.2 (pp. 39ÔÇô43); E. Seneta,
*Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006,
┬ğ1.2 (pp. 27ÔÇô28) for the underlying PerronÔÇôFrobenius theorem.

### Spin-`S` saturated ferromagnetic state (Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 generalised)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki ┬ğ2.4 P1i for the
**saturated ferromagnet**: the all-aligned (constant-spin) basis
state `|¤â_ÔèñÔş® = Ôèù_x |cÔş®` with `¤â x = c` for all `x : V`. The two
extremal weights `c = 0` (highest weight, "all up") and
`c = Fin.last N` (lowest weight, "all down") are the highest- and
lowest-weight vectors of the `J_tot = |V|┬ÀS = |V|┬ÀN/2` irreducible
SU(2) representation in the multi-site Hilbert space. Tracked in
Issue #412; assembled in PRs #875ÔÇô#879. All theorems live in
`Quantum/SpinS/AllAlignedState.lean`.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `allAlignedConfigS V N c` | constant configuration `¤â x = c` (PR #875) |
| `allAlignedStateS V N c` | basis state at constant `c`, equal to `basisVecS (allAlignedConfigS V N c)` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magSumS = |V|┬Àc.val` (PR #875) |
| `magEigenvalueS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magEigenvalueS = |V|┬ÀN/2 ÔêÆ |V|┬Àc` (PR #875) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_allAlignedStateS` | `┼£^z_tot ┬À |cÔş® = (|V|┬ÀN/2 ÔêÆ |V|┬Àc) ┬À |cÔş®` for any `c` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | `c = 0` Ôş╣ `magSumS = 0` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_pos_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | the all-up configuration is the **unique** `magSumS = 0` configuration (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_last` | `c = Fin.last N` Ôş╣ `magSumS = |V|┬ÀN` (PR #876) |
| `magSumS_lt_card_mul_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_last` | the all-down configuration is the unique configuration with `magSumS = |V|┬ÀN` (PR #876) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | the **all-up state is a Heisenberg eigenvector for ANY coupling** ÔÇö magnetization conservation `[H, ┼£^z_tot] = 0` + uniqueness of the M=0 configuration (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_eigenvalue` | explicit Heisenberg eigenvalue formula on all-up: `╬ú_x J(x,x)┬ÀN(N+2)/4 + ╬ú_{xÔëáy} J(x,y)┬ÀN┬▓/4` (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` / `_eigenvalue` | symmetric c = N (all-down) Heisenberg eigenvector + same eigenvalue formula (PR #876) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpPlus_apply_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | `(onSiteS x ┼£^+) ¤â' ¤â_Ôèñ = 0` (PR #877) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpPlus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | `(onSiteS x ┼£^+).mulVec |¤â_ÔèñÔş® = 0` (PR #877) |
| `totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | **`┼£^+_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş® = 0`** (highest-weight annihilation, PR #877) |
| `onSiteS_spinSOpMinus_apply_allAlignedConfigS_last` / `_mulVec_` / `totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric lowest-weight annihilation `┼£^-_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèÑÔş® = 0` (PR #877) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | the all-up state is a `(┼£_tot)┬▓`-eigenvector (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_apply_diag_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | explicit Casimir diagonal value `|V|┬ÀN(N+2)/4 + (|V|┬▓ÔêÆ|V|)┬ÀN┬▓/4` (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_eigenvalue` | **`(┼£_tot)┬▓ ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş® = (|V|┬ÀN/2)┬À(|V|┬ÀN/2 + 1) ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®`** ÔÇö operator-level form of "all-up is the highest-weight vector of the J_tot = |V|┬ÀS irreducible SU(2) representation" (PR #878) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` / `_apply_diag_` / `_eigenvalue` | symmetric lowest-weight Casimir eigenvalue (same value) (PR #879) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_commute_totalSpinSOp1` / `_Op2` / `_OpPlus` / `_OpMinus` | `Commute`-form conversions: H commutes with each axis-total operator (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_commute_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow` / `_Plus_pow` | iterated power Commute by induction (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for any k, `(┼£^-_tot)^k ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®` is a Heisenberg eigenvector at the same eigenvalue as `|¤â_ÔèñÔş®` (PR #881) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric for `┼£^+_tot` on all-down (PR #881) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_commute_totalSpinSOp1` / `_Op2` / `_OpPlus` / `_OpMinus` / `_OpMinus_pow` / `_OpPlus_pow` | Casimir Commute-form analogues (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero` | for any k, `(┼£^-_tot)^k ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®` preserves the Casimir eigenvalue `(|V|┬ÀN/2)┬À(|V|┬ÀN/2+1)` (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSSquared_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric (PR #882) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_commutator_totalSpinSOpMinus` | multi-site Cartan: `[┼£^z_tot, ┼£^-_tot] = -┼£^-_tot` (PR #883) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_commutator_totalSpinSOpPlus` | multi-site Cartan: `[┼£^z_tot, ┼£^+_tot] = +┼£^+_tot` (PR #883) |
| `magConfigS_zero_eq_allAlignedConfigS` / `magConfigS_card_zero` / `magConfigS_zero_instNonempty` | the `M = 0` magnetization sector contains exactly the all-up configuration `allAlignedConfigS V N 0`; cardinality 1; non-empty (PR #885, file `Quantum/SpinS/MagConfigExtremalCardinality.lean`) |
| `magConfigS_last_eq_allAlignedConfigS` / `magConfigS_card_last` / `magConfigS_last_instNonempty` | symmetric `M = |V|┬ÀN` sector contains exactly the all-down configuration `allAlignedConfigS V N (Fin.last N)`; cardinality 1; non-empty (PR #885) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | single-step magnetic-quantum-number shift: `┼£^z_tot ┬À (┼£^-_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®) = (|V|┬ÀN/2 ÔêÆ 1) ┬À (┼£^-_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®)` ÔÇö the once-lowered all-up state is an `┼£^z_tot` eigenvector with magnetic quantum number `m_max ÔêÆ 1` (PR #886) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric: `┼£^z_tot ┬À (┼£^+_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèÑÔş®) = (ÔêÆ|V|┬ÀN/2 + 1) ┬À (┼£^+_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèÑÔş®)` (PR #886) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_eigenvec` / `_OpPlus_mulVec_eigenvec` | generic single-step shift on any `┼£^z_tot` eigenvector: `┼£^z_tot ¤ê = ╬╗ ¤ê` ÔçÆ `┼£^z_tot (┼£^Ôêô_tot ¤ê) = (╬╗ Ôêô 1) (┼£^Ôêô_tot ¤ê)`. Proven via the multi-site Cartan rearrangement `┼£^z_tot ┬À ┼£^Ôêô_tot = ┼£^Ôêô_tot ┬À ┼£^z_tot Ôêô ┼£^Ôêô_tot` lifted to `mulVec` (PR #887) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero` | **iterated magnetic-quantum-number labelling** `┼£^z_tot ┬À ((┼£^-_tot)^k ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®) = (|V|┬ÀN/2 ÔêÆ k) ┬À ((┼£^-_tot)^k ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®)` for every `k : Ôäò`. Inducts at the eigenvector level using the generic single-step shift `_eigenvec`, bypassing the technically delicate operator-level iterated Cartan (PR #887) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last` | symmetric for `(┼£^+_tot)^k ┬À |¤â_ÔèÑÔş®` with eigenvalue `ÔêÆ|V|┬ÀN/2 + k` (PR #887) |
| `magSubspaceS_eq_eigenspace` / `magSubspaceS_iSupIndep` / `magSubspaceS_isInternal` | spin-`S` magnetization subspaces form an internal direct sum decomposition: bridge to `Module.End.eigenspace`, distinct-eigenvalue independence (via `Module.End.eigenspaces_iSupIndep` over Ôäé), combined with the existing `iSup_magSubspaceS_eq_top` (PR #889, file `Quantum/SpinS/MagnetizationDirectSum.lean`) |
| `totalSpinSOpMinus_pow_allAlignedStateS_zero_mem_magSubspaceS` / `totalSpinSOpPlus_pow_allAlignedStateS_last_mem_magSubspaceS` | PR #887 ladder iterates lie in the magnetization sectors `magSubspaceS V N (m_max Ôêô k)` (PR #889 corollaries) |
| `oneFlippedUpConfig V x_0 hN` / `oneFlippedDownConfig V x_0 hN` | one-flipped configurations: `0 ÔåÆ 1` at site `x_0` (resp. `N ÔåÆ N-1`), all other sites at `0` (resp. `N`); requires `0 < N` (PR #890, file `Quantum/SpinS/LadderIterateNonvanishing.lean`) |
| `totalSpinSOpMinus_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_at_oneFlippedUpConfig` | explicit value `((┼£^-_tot ┬À |¤â_ÔèñÔş®)) (oneFlippedUpConfig V x_0) = ÔêÜN`. Proof distributes via `Matrix.sum_mulVec`, isolates only the pivot site `x_0`, reduces via `spinSOpMinus_apply_lower N (0 + 1 = 1) = ÔêÜ(N ┬À 1)` (PR #890) |

### Single-mode fermion (P2 skeleton)

Phase 2 entry point: the canonical anticommutation algebra of a single
fermion mode acting on `Ôäé┬▓` with computational basis
`|0Ôş®` (vacuum) and `|1Ôş®` (occupied).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `fermionAnnihilation` | `c = !![0, 1; 0, 0] = |0Ôş®Ôş¿1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation` | `cÔÇá = !![0, 0; 1, 0] = |1Ôş®Ôş¿0|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber` | `n = !![0, 0; 0, 1] = |1Ôş®Ôş¿1|` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_eq_creation_mul_annihilation` | `n = cÔÇá ┬À c` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_sq` | `c┬▓ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_sq` | `(cÔÇá)┬▓ = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnticomm_self` | `c ┬À cÔÇá + cÔÇá ┬À c = 1` (single-mode CAR) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_sq` | `n┬▓ = n` (idempotent number operator) | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_conjTranspose` | `cß┤┤ = cÔÇá` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_conjTranspose` | `(cÔÇá)ß┤┤ = c` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_isHermitian` | `n` is Hermitian | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionVacuum`, `fermionOccupied` | basis vectors `|0Ôş® = (1, 0)`, `|1Ôş® = (0, 1)` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionAnnihilation_mulVec_vacuum` / `_occupied` | `c|0Ôş® = 0`, `c|1Ôş® = |0Ôş®` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionCreation_mulVec_vacuum` / `_occupied` | `cÔÇá|0Ôş® = |1Ôş®`, `cÔÇá|1Ôş® = 0` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |
| `fermionNumber_mulVec_vacuum` / `_occupied` | `n|0Ôş® = 0`, `n|1Ôş® = |1Ôş®` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |

| `fermionCreation_eq_spinHalfOpMinus` | `cÔÇá = ¤â^-` | `Fermion/Mode.lean` |

| `fermionCreation_eq_spinSOpMinus_one` | `cÔÇá = spinSOpMinus 1` | `Fermion/SpinSBridge.lean` (PR #936) |

| `fermionAnnihilation_mul_fermionCreation_mulVec_vacuum` / `_occupied` | `(c ┬À cÔÇá) ┬À |0Ôş® = |0Ôş®`; `(c ┬À cÔÇá) ┬À |1Ôş® = 0` (vacuum/occupied as eigenstates of `c ┬À cÔÇá`) | `Fermion/CCDaggerAction.lean` (PR #966) |

| `fermionNumber_pow_succ` / `fermionAnnihilation_mul_fermionCreation_pow_succ` | `n^(k+1) = n`; `(c ┬À cÔÇá)^(k+1) = c ┬À cÔÇá` for any `k : Ôäò` (positive-degree power identities of the idempotent projections) | `Fermion/ProjectionPow.lean` (PR #992) |
| `fermionMultiNumber_anticommutator_fermionMultiAnnihilation_self` / `fermionMultiNumber_anticommutator_fermionMultiCreation_self` | `{n_i, c_i} = c_i`; `{n_i, c_iÔÇá} = c_iÔÇá` (multi-mode JW same-site ladder anticommutators, mirror of PR #990) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/NumberAnticommutators.lean` (PR #993) |
